If you want a truly mobile set-up, you might find that the best option isn't a telescope at all. Invest in a nice pair of binoculars or a spotting scope that will fit nicely in a backpack, and there will still be plenty for you to see. You don't have to worry about size restraints! Since portability isn't going to be a huge issue for you, feel free to go as big as you want. 12" Meade? 20" Dobsonian? Bring it on. Cool, so you probably want a decently portable telescope. Any telescope is portable if you try hard enough, but you'll have the easiest time with something medium-to-small sized, like a NexStar SE or a StarSense 102.Alright. Gotta pack some snacks. How many bags of chips do you need? * (link: "Just one - you’ll have the most fun observing by yourself.")[(set: $crowd to "<mark>''Observing:''</mark> Since you’ll be mostly observing by yourself, make sure you can handle the entire set-up and take-down process alone!")(go-to: "Q3: Target")] * (link: "A couple - you have a few friends who want to come along.")[(set: $crowd to "<mark>''Observing:''</mark> If you’ve got a group with you – especially if there are kids there – it can be annoying having to spend a long time setting up and finding objects. Consider getting a tracking mount, so that multiple people can look at an object back-to-back and you won’t have to step in to adjust the aim as the sky moves. There are also options for projecting the telescope’s image onto a screen for easier viewing!")(go-to: "Q3: Target")] * (link: "As many as possible - friends, family, neighbors - everyone’s going to want to come and take a look.")[(set: $crowd to "<mark>''Observing:''</mark> If you’ve got a big group with you – especially if there are kids there – it can be annoying having to spend a long time setting up and finding objects. Consider getting a tracking mount, so that multiple people can look at an object back-to-back and you won’t have to step in to adjust the aim as the sky moves. a party! If you're going to have a lot of folks wanting to look through the scope, a tracking mount might be helpful, as you won't have to keep adjusting the aim between observers. Ah, a solo mission. In that case, either a tracking mount or a manual mount will be totally fine - just a matter of personal preference. If you have a few people wanting to look through the telescope with you, it might help to have some technological assistance to get you up and running. A phone-integrated scope (say, one from Celestron's StarSense line) will give you a nice blend of computer aid and manual control!Once you get your gear set up, you’re most excited to look at… * (link: "The planets! Jupiter’s moons and Saturn’s rings are the most fascinating.")[(set: $target to "<mark>''Targets:''</mark> Planetary observing means you need //magnification//. A bigger aperture is better, as it will allow you to see smaller details. You can also look into colored filters to enhance the contrast!")(go-to: "Q4: Nav")] * (link: "Some deep sky objects like galaxies and nebulae, in all their wispy, abstract glory.")[(set: $target to "<mark>''Targets:''</mark> Deep-sky objects are gorgeous, but often very dim. To see them best, you need to collect as much of their light as possible, which means you need the biggest aperture possible. Refractors, which have higher contrast than reflectors, can also help, though they tend to be much smaller per dollar, so it’s a trade-off. Contrast filters can be added to help to bring out things like nebulae.")(go-to: "Q4: Nav")] * (link: "How about both?")[(set: $target to "<mark>''Targets:''</mark> You want it all! A Schmidt-Cassegrain telescope might be the thing for you. It’s a jack-of-all-trades style of optics that will perform well observing both planets and deep sky objects. Would you like to use your telescope to look at things //besides// the night sky? * (link: "Terrestrial viewing would be nice!")[(set: $extras to "<mark>''Terrestrial Observing:''</mark> Not all telescopes display an image that is right-side-up and flipped the correct horizontal direction. This is because in space, there isn’t really an \"up,\" so it doesn’t matter! However, if you want to use your scope to look at boats in the harbor or whales in the sound, you need to make sure that the image will be oriented correctly. Stay away from Dobsonians, which will always be the wrong way around, in addition to being hard to point at the horizon.")(go-to: "Summary")] * (link: "How about the daytime sky? Solar observing sounds awesome.")[(set: $extras to "<mark>''Solar:''</mark> Solar observing is its own category, and there are lots of awesome dedicated solar telescopes that really let you see our Sun in all its glory. However, you can also stick a solar filter onto the front of any regular telescope! It’s just a matter of finding one in the right size.")(go-to: "Summary")] * (link: "Both terrestrial and solar, please!")[(set: $extras to "<mark>''Terrestrial and Solar Observing:''</mark> Not all telescopes display an image that is right-side-up and flipped the correct horizontal direction. This is because in space, there isn’t really an \"up,\" so it doesn’t matter! However, if you want to use your scope to look at boats in the harbor or whales in the sound, you need to make sure that the image will be oriented correctly. Stay away from Dobsonians, which will always be the wrong way around, in addition to being hard to point at the horizon. As for solar observing, it’s kind of its own category, and there are lots of awesome dedicated solar telescopes that really let you see our Sun in all its glory. However, you can also stick a solar filter onto the front of any regular telescope! It’s just a matter of finding one in the right size.")(go-to: "Summary")] * (link: "Nah, the night sky is what I really want to see.")[(set: $extras to "no")(go-to: "Summary")] <img align="right" Spending time outside watching the night sky is its own reward.")[(set: $photos to "<mark>''Photography:''</mark> If you’re not worried about setting up a camera, you’re free to use either a tracking mount or a manual mount. If you ever decide you want to take some quick snapshots with your telescope, you can always add a mounting device that will let you take pictures with your phone’s camera!")(go-to: "Extras")] * (link: "Photos! You want to take gorgeous images of galaxies and planets to remember them by.")[(set: $photos to "<mark>''Photography:''</mark> If astrophotography sounds like the rabbit hole for you, you’ll want to invest in an equatorial mount. These track the sky while matching the angle of the Earth’s rotation, so that you can take super long exposures and really capture all the detail of those dim deep-sky objects. Planetary photography has a slightly different process, but will also require a tracking mount. If picking out all the individual pieces seems overwhelming, you might check out a \"smart\" telescope, many of which come with built-in photography capabilities!")(go-to: "Extras")] <img
